I requested an intermediate SUV (like a Nissan Rogue) and got a Jeep Compass - which is sub-standard to a Rogue... This was on a Tuesday at 1pm - they not only had no other comparable SUV's, they did not even have an Intermediate or Full Size car to trade out to (that has more trunk room than the Jeep Compass!) I rented the car a day before needing it, and in the 24 hours prior to departing, no other cars came in, acquired or offered to obtain the driving experience hoped for. < Review>
I live in Natomas, but I make the trip to Rancho Cordova because NOBODY waxes away my "beard and mustache" like Miranda! Whenever I leave, my face feels smoother than a baby's butt and --this is what's important-- that smoothness LASTS for two or even three weeks! I'd tried several of the other ladies before I connected with Miranda, and that's what you have to do to find the tech who works best for you. (When I m moved from RC to Natomas, I tried the local EWC, and wasn't happy with the results, so I decided to just bite it and stick with Miranda, instead of trying to fit with another tech.) All of the techs I saw at RC (four others before Miranda) were very friendly and professional. The place is always clean and they've FINALLY got a REGULAR front desk staff that is very pleasant (it wasn't always that way--there used to the a revolving door up there!), Cajun being my favorite.  Another thing I like about EWC is that they don't have some BS policy of charging you if you miss your appointment. And if you're running late, they allow you up to nine minutes past your appointment time before they just go to the next person--no big deal.

The only negative I have is that I didn't appreciate that they DO NOT inform you about the "touch up policy." If your hair grows back within a couple days after waxing, you can go in for a rewax FOR FREE. This is important to know ESPECIALLY when you first start waxing because the hair does grows back really fast until, as they explain, all the hair gets into a regular growth cycle. I always buy bundled packages (they call them  "Passes") and I was going back and USING my passes, because no one told me about the touch up policy until I complained to the Manager (who DID tell me) about the hair coming back too fast. So now YOU know.

Overall I love the place and highly recommend the RC location.< /Review>

< text>
Don't even think of installing solar panels until you have talked to Eric at PacSolar. From the beginning he was clear, informative and accurate. He gave me a price over a year prior to our remodel and ended up doing the job for less. He answers the phone, comes out and deals with you directly and gets on the roof with his excellent crew. He also handles all the paperwork and liaison with PG&E and the permits. If I could put more than five stars I would

<text>We just got solar installed by Pac Solar and it was a very smooth and easy process from start to finish. Eric is meticulous in his attention to detail and was able to educate us on all of our options and design the most logical system for our needs. After our first meeting he provided a proposal about one week later and when I researched the panels and inverters that he uses I learned that they are the best ones available on the market which was good to see. He isn't trying to save $ by using cheap materials. <UserId.>105232450472778351626< /UserId.><username>Russell Feirstein<//username>< date>
1421260049030< /date>
<rate>5<//rate><text>When you buy into solar energy, you pick a point in time, preferably while rebates exist. Right now, at 30% federal tax credit (which big solar companies TAKE to reduce their costs, not yours),  the cost of solar finally got down to a relative sweet spot finally. Yes, the technology will change for the better, same with cars. You just have to pick the best time for "you" to buy.  With any solar installation, there are up-front costs. But PAC works on providing you with the payback in years for the saved energy at current PGE costs. PGE always inflates their energy pricing (2 - 3%/year), so it often is "less than what's calculated", if you generalize and project a 5.5 to 5.8 year payback at a static energy cost.

Installation is explained well in terms of where conduits will be run for maximum appeal and shortest run where DC voltage loss is lowest. Eric explains why or why not you would benefit from a string inverter vs. a set of micro-inverters, and makes good sense, after analyzing shading areas, obstructions and trees or neighbor's long chimney shadow in winter at 4 PM that may reduce overall output. All these items add-up. The other solar companies don't go up on your roof with you and "look around" for such things that could reduce your photon count to the projected installation area.

Overall, the purchase and installation process was well done, well engineered, and a full and complete disclosure of the entire process and how it was designed, installed, warrantied for parts/labor, and configured for grid tie in, PGE rate schedules, city permitting and sign off, was all presented in a neatly organized binder for reference and any possible future warranty or post-installation service.< /text>< Pics>

<rate>5< /rate>< review>
If words like kilowatts, inverters, and conduit do not fall trippingly off your tongue, you need someone to explain how solar works, how the costs and savings stack up, and how the system can connect to your home's existing electrical system.  Eric Miller is the guy who can explain this to you (more than once if necessary).  Unlike our first bid, Eric got up on the roof and measured exactly how the panels would fit in between our roof vents, and he produced a drawing of the layout.  He also looked at our electrical panel, and immediately knew we needed a subpanel (more space) for the connection.  That turned out to be a simple item, but one the other vendor's salesperson could not fathom.

Installation was very professional.  The guys on the roof used a ladder support to protect my rain gutters where the ladder rested.  They took great care to measure the joist locations, so the support feet would be in the exact right location.   It is unnerving to hear anyone drilling holes in your roof, but the triple rain protection they install is a belt-and-suspenders approach.  The guy installing the subpanel was similarly careful, and he did a beautiful job routing the conduit that leads to the roof.

Eric makes a very important final visit to teach you how to monitor your system's electricity production, which is available realtime.  He even gives you a draft tax form to claim your tax credit!

I really don't think anyone will beat the service and knowledge of Pac Solar.  I am very satisfied with this purchase.< /review>

< review>
The selection of a Solar company that I could trust with the design, installation, and maintenance of a Solar Electric Photovoltaic System has been a roller coaster ride. I first started looking around for some quotes in the summer of 2015. I had many sales‚Äô visits and site inspections from different companies, during which I gather data and research the true cost of Solar. What struck me is that every salesman I talked to had an elaborate ROI calculation that seemed dubious (at best) and were putting a lot of pressure to sign contracts during the first visit. Also some companies preferred string inverters while others praised micro-inverters. While I much preferred micro-inverters, the prices quoted were ridiculously high. So I decided to put the project on hold.

Until one day I read a post about a neighbor recommending Pac Solar and decided to give Eric Miller a call. It was not long after our first call that Eric came for a site inspection and we talked at length about component brands, system size, warranties, etc. Having an EE background, it was refreshing to talk to someone who could actually answer my questions! Eric came back a few days later with a proposal backed with a comprehensive document explaining the choice of components, the process of  permitting and installation, warranty, prices, and timeline laid out in a totally transparent way.

Before signing off, I decided to do my due diligence and talked to a friend working in the energy industry (also an electrical engineer). He confirm the choice of micro-inverters and panels as the best in the industry today, a claim backed by an internal review his company did to evaluate performance and efficiency of components over time. So I decided to go for it.

I was extremely pleased by the service, the workmanship, and the attention to details throughout the design, installation, and review process. Eric has always been very responsive in returning calls and and got the job done according to schedule.

The best part of it is that my system will pay itself off in 5 years! How is that? Because the system was properly sized to my electricity needs. If you only compare the price per Watt, you might be thinking ‚Äúyea this is more expensive per Watt than company X or Y‚Äù. But this is the wrong way to look at it. Keep in mind that an oversized Solar PV System using a string inverter will be much more expensive out the door and will take 2-3 times longer to pay off benefitting only the Solar vendor. What you need to be looking for is the total price of the system and how long it will take to pay it off (everything else being equal).</review>

<Text>My elderly mother (82 year old) recently went to this store requesting assistance for difficulties she was having with her mobile phone and wanting information about how to get it replaced via the insurance that she was paying for. NATE was unable to answer her questions and although there was no one else in the store, he was impatient and treated an elderly Asian woman in a disrespectful manner by telling her to "Get out of here", "Leave the store", and "Shoo" as if she was annoying animal. I see from the reviews here that many customers are treated well and are satisfied with the service and so it suggests that my mother was targeted for some reason based on her race, gender, age, accent or other factors. <Name>Fern Mora</Name>< date>
1561517884923</date>
<rating>3< /rating>< review>
The Hermosa Beach Pier promenade is a happening place to visit. The location of the Tower 12 restaurant has been around for a long time but under another name.  It has been a local hangout where locals go during the week. Tourist flock there on weekends to hang out upstairs at one of their 2 bars and scope out the bikini babes below on Pier's walking promenade. If your in to  beers and  burgers  type places them this is your place. It can get pretty loud on holidays and weekends. But then most of the restaurants on Pier do also. If your looking for a quiet romantic place looking for that California sunset, this is not for you. Swimsuit and flip-flops are the norm. Their single cheese burger has 2 beef patties and the double cheese burger has 3 they say because the patties are thin. They do however have a good happy hour with 32oz tap beers and 22oz mixed drinks.

A Local Patron<//review>

< Review>
They have deal of one free pizza per 10 people. The pizza is about 9 inches in diameter and the only half priced drinks are fishbowls (totally worth it if you don't have work the next day). My group ordered the stuff crust which had mixed reviews between us. It's an ALL ricotta and herbs mix inside of what is basically a bread roll affixed to paper thin crust. The wings are awesome, with perfect "hot wing sauce". Their naughty mermaid drink is nice and light.</Review>

< Text>
If I could rate this place 0 stars I would. Unfortunately, this review is based on the culture of this establishment and not on its food. BOTTOM LINE THIS PLACE IS A RACIST ESTABLISHMENT so I definitely WOULD NOT RECOMMEND anyone to it for sure. On 6/2/17 I nicely went up to the gentlemen at the door and asked if they were letting anyone else in and he politely said no. At this point I didn't think anything of it since it was close to 1.  What I saw after is what pissed me off. They let two separate groups of white folks in right after they said they weren't letting anyone else in. That's BS to me. My group of friends watched this all go down... they wouldn't let a group of black and asian folks go in but they sure let white folks go in. I was super disappointed to say the least as I love going to Hermosa Beach and frequent there often. I have never come across this type of behavior at other establishments on the pier. I thought it was important and necessary to say something to the gentlemen I previously spoke with. As I walked back to try to speak to him,  he was acting like he didn't see me even though I was the only person in the vicinity along with the doorman. Since he wasn't trying to talk to me, I told the doorman in a professional manner that it was disappointing to see them letting people in after they just told me they weren't letting anyone else in. At this point the gentlemen decided to make a statement and defend himself saying it's not what you think. I reiterate that it doesn't look good when you just told me you weren't letting people in and immediately after let a group of white folks in but deny entrance to people of various ethnic backgrounds. His defense was they were service industry people. Sorry buddy that excuse doesn't fly especially when two separate groups go in from two separate areas. I've worked years in the service industry so I can acknowledge that we would frequent other bars after our shift ends but not in the manner that these folks were dressed. Cmon y'all knew what you were doing ... let's be real here. I don't use the word racist lightly when accusing someone of it without merit. I would hands down say STAY AWAY FROM THIS ESTABLISHMENT ... super disappointing.<//Text>
